< review>
I thoroughly enjoyed my visits to Peach Tree Vision. It was my first time getting glasses, and at nearing thirty I was giddy like a child due to always having wanted glasses. They all genuinely enjoyed my excitement and I didn't feel judged or frowned upon in the slightest. They were very patient, helpful, informative, and made me feel welcome every time I was there. I plan on going back in soon to buy another pair or two as backups. I was also never pressured to buy glasses from them and was given an honest answer when I asked if I was able to take my prescription anywhere to buy glasses. Although I could have gone elsewhere with it, I chose to buy my glasses there in the end. They are very affordable. My insurance covered the exam, so I am not sure of the price range there, but as for the glasses themselves  I believe the each pair is $40 if I remember correctly. This was well over a year ago, so don't quote me due to my potential memory lapse or potential changes they may have made. I highly recommend this place! The glasses themselves have held up perfectly, as well.</review>

<text>Location/Atmosphere
Had a very romantic vibe! Perhaps a good place to have a date night with your spouse?
The table outside are nice but there really isn't much to long at aside from people walking by.

Food
Most of the food was fairly good, however, the desert portion was fairly disappointing.

Brushetta Di Pomodori---
Perhaps my favorite part of the entire meal? The Bruschetta disappeared from the table almost instantaneously. The kids kept asking for more....
Insalate Piccolo----
The salad was absolutely amazing! I loved the taste of the gorgonzola cheese and the salad had just the right chunks of avocado. My only suggestion is for the salad to be served with more pieces of dried cranberry. Other than that, I would definitely order this salad again! Oh, I do believe that it is filling enough to be ordered as a main entree.
Linguine Alle Vongole--
I love the spicy after taste of this pasta! It had just the right amount of garlic and clams. The pasta was simple but fulfilled it's purpose and was as described by the waiters.
--Desert--
Was rather disappointed in the deserts, we ordered the Tiramisu and plate of cannoli's.
Tiramisu--
Not going to lie, I was very disappointed with the Tiramisu. It tasted more like cake than actual Tiramisu. I've had better Tiramisu at Safeway.....
Cannoli Alla Ricotta--
The cheese and cream was okay, nothing special. The Cannoli's were hard and perhaps overcooked?

Prices
Definitely not cheap!

Service/Staff
The servers were very professional and attentive. However, the female server seemed to be in a rush whenever she was speaking or stopping by the table.

I may or may not be going back to this place. Perhaps for a date night but not with the kids. The place was expensive, more of a "once in a while treat". Definitely tasty though and worth the visit.....< /text><pictures>None</pictures><Resp>None</Resp><GmapID>0x808fa4af962d1ed7:0x5f6905656124d39a</GmapID></record>

<text>My boyfriend took me here for Valentine's Day. He made a reservation for 8pm and we arrived at 7:54pm. The tiny place was packed and there was no room for waiting customers. There were 3 other couples waiting and some of them had to wait outside in the cold because of the lack of space. When 8:05pm came, there were still no available tables and nobody communicated how much longer we had to wait, so everyone just stood there. A table opened up at 8:15ish and there was confusion as to who should be seated first since the other couples also had the same reservations.

When we got a table, they forgot to give us bread. I know they were extremely busy and understaffed, but that just made the experience worse. I ordered the homemade fettuccine with spicy tomato sauce and prawns. I didn't enjoy it, but my boyfriend liked his cheese and pear filled pasta. The dessert was the highlight for me. We had the tiramisu which wasn't too sweet nor overwhelming.

That first experience turned me off so I would suggest NOT going here during peak days like Valentine's.</text>< Pics>

<Text>Piccolo is probably my new favorite Italian Restaurant.  My boyfriend and I decided to try it one night after driving by it a few times and seeing it constantly packed with patrons.

Appetizer: Avocado Salad ($10)
We split an Avocado Salad. as our appetizer.  It was a pretty large portion and they served it to us in two plates without us asking which was very thoughtful! One salad was enough for two and we loved the honey mustard  dressing!

Main Dishes: Fiocchetti con Pere ($15) &  Fettuccine con gamberi ($17)
On the menu "Fiocchetti con Pere" is described as "homemade ribbons pasta filled with cheese, pear and gorgonzola sauce" and is apparently the restaurant's signature dish. We went with our server's recommendation and ordered this; however, she mentioned that it did not have pear in it. I'm not sure if they ran out of pear or changed the recipe but we were not given an explanation.  Hopefully they will have it with pear next time we visit.  Still, it was very delicious.  I am not a huge cheese person so my boyfriend finished the dish for me and I ate his Fettuccine con Gamberi which was also quite tasty.

Dessert: Panna Cotta (Passionfruit)
Even though we stuffed ourselves with the large portion sizes we still left room for dessert and shared the passionfruit Panna Cotta.

We will definitely be back for another visit and to try more items on the list.  It is a bit pricey but you definitely get the quality that you pay for.</Text><resp>None</resp></record>

MikeG< /user_name>
< Time>
1575825476028< /Time>
<Rating>4< /Rating>< text>
Spoke with the owner when I was there with the family and they're open consistently now along with an "OPEN" sign.  Excellent food, loved it and so did the wife.  Tried the Picana beef plate, didn't realize it was grass fed beef.  I say this as for those who have not tried grass fed beef it can be tough, but extremely flavorful and a bonus is that it is healthier, look it up.  When eating grass fed beef, cut into smaller bite size pieces and it will be fine. Definitely not tender like wagyu (Japanese beef) so don't expect it, just a different type of beef.
Wife had the chicken stroganoff, which was delicious, along with a side of beef pastel, yummy.  Pastel is a bit like Indian samosa except very light crust filled with meat and not spicy.
Owner gave us a free side of beans to try and it was delicious.  Staff is very accommodating and attentive.  We did have a side of fried bananas that we had forgotten about and was delivered late, was comped the plate without even asking.  Love this about small owner operated restaurants, typically much better service.
Will I be back again, of course and many times more.< /text>

A beautiful canyon open space to explore< /review>
<pictures>None</pictures><Resp>None<//Resp><gmap_id>0x80d9547ed5ac9beb:0x834029467576d39b</gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
< rate>

< user>
106801717568154343538<//user>
<user_name>James J. Griffin<//user_name>< Gmap_id>
0x80d9547ed5ac9beb:0x834029467576d39b<//Gmap_id>
<Date>1448121412969</Date><Pictures>None< /Pictures><response>None<//response>< text>
Living in the Burlingame neighborhood, Juniper canyon is a piece of open space that figures heavily in my dog walking cycle.

As opposed to nearby Switzer Canyon which is a great spot for a picnic, or to read, meditate, think, imbibe, whatever, Juniper Canyon is a thin walking trail / wash. You're not going to find much area aside right off Juniper street where you can hang out for any extended period of time.

If you enter from the Juniper side, it's a slight uphill walk through a wash up to the exit past the signage on Nutmeg street. It is certainly a wash though, and any type of rain is going to produce a muddy running water mess. This has resulted in some pretty serious ruts and exposed river rock. Ankles beware. Especially if your dog is like mine and likes to pull.

There is an access road off of Maple street if you feel like climbing your way out of the canyon early, but that's up the side and is pretty steep.<//text>

<Text>I was new to Fremont and needed a salon near me. Needless to say, got tired of constantly going to another city to get my haircut. Vintage Styles was recommended to me so I went to give them a try.

First, I was really impressed with how friendly the entire staff is. It was far different and way better than any other barbershop or salon I've ever visited. Everyone here was welcoming and treated every visitor, myself included, like a part of their family.

Second, I was also pretty impressed by the variety of services they had at the salon. I thought it was just a hair salon, but -- to my surprise -- they actually function as a full-service salon. I noticed they do spa services and manicures as well.

Third, my haircut turned out great. As a male, I'm generally nervous trying out new hair salons because I'm not sure if they mostly specialize in women's hair styling or men's, but was pretty happy to see they actually have a really diverse customer base and are great at everything they do!

My favorite buffet place! Always visit whenever we are in Vegas. So many dishes to choose and the freshness of oyster and crab legs are no doubt! It's really a buffet place for everyone, for those who likes a glass (or two) wine (or beer) with their food, wine - mimosa and beer are included. For those who has a sweet tooth like me - desserts sections are heavenly, you name it.. from pizza, pasta, salad, fried chicken, mac n cheese, prime rib, asian, soups, fresh oysters, crab legs, they are all in there. But be aware.. their seafood buffet only on Friday night, and all day for Saturdays and Sundays. Tips.. come on Friday around 1.30-ish so you get to pay for Brunch price, and by 2.30pm they already change the menu to seafood buffet. But why come at 1.30 you asked? Because the line is no joke!</text>

<review>This place has a wide variety of fast food meals that taste delicious. Nothing is microwaved or reheated and everything has quality ingredients considering it's fast food. The orders come out pretty quickly. There's a lot of condiments inside. This is the SPOT in LCR! Affordable prices too.
What an amazing hidden gem located in Montrose! This restaurant specializes in Nashville Style Fried Chicken that is made fresh to order. I came here over the weekend with a group of people and had the luxury to taste the food.
The Fried Chicken is absolutely delicious. The chicken was very moist and tender. You can adjust the spicy level from no spice all the way up to blazin. You can order the chicken as a slider or a tender with sides of fries and cole slaw.
The staff is very friendly and attentive and will help you guide through the process. I would definitely recommend this restaurant to anyone who is in need of good food!< /review><pictures>None< /pictures>< response>

<review>Comcast retail apparently thinks that it is okay to make people wait for 1/2 hour - 1 hour to change out equipment that we pay anywhere from $2-$10 a month for.  These are not complex problems.  You swap it out.  When I asked to a manager, ERIC told me that he was sorta the manager.   And then I told him I was disgusted that out of 9 stations, 2 were servicing people and he and his co-worker were laughing and talking in the front desk.  He said he just got to work and that he had things to do before helping people.  7 people walked into the store after me.  It was a sudden entrance of people.  I was #5.  You do the math.  Each person takes 10 minutes or so.  Worse than the DMV.  IN fact, I rather go to the DMV.  Here is some suggestions...typical queuing theory (many lines versus one line).

1.  Track what issues you have and how long each case takes.
2.  If there is an obvious issue that goes quick like simply swapping out equipment,  then create a separate line or even a window where all the equipment is available right there, on shelves ready to go.  Have people queue up in that line to get just new equipment.
3.  To decide the issue, ask questions upon the customer entering.  You already have the desk and a nifty tool to enter the name of the customer.  This seems to happen but inconsistently.
4.  Make sure there is more than two employees working.  You charge a lot, a lot of money for your service, you can hire people.  Your retail stores are large and you have 9, count them 9 stations in your Sunnyvale store.  The incremental cost of hiring an employee is at this point, just the employee.  It is not as if you need a bigger store.
5.  No laughing, no ignoring customers, no talking.  This is serious.  People have things to do, places to be.   Please don't insult us by talking and not taking the job seriously (ERIC)
6.  Study your stream of customers, understand peak and non-peak hours.  Make sure you are staffed for it correctly.
7.  I want to see a employees calling for help when they see the line gets too long.  Even Safeway or Trader Joe's does that.  Please visit the stores to see how this works.
8.  Cross train your employees so they can do multiple jobs so in the case of a burst of customers, someone can bring the line down.   In other words, Trader Joe's got this one down big time.  Anyone at their stores can ring up someone.  I will hand you that your system is more complicated than a grocery store but hire smarter people.

It really feels as Comcast does not understand customer service 101. You have a good service, you have apparently now good service call times with a small window.  Get the retail up to par.

You have a monopoly in our area.  All other service is subpar compared to yours.  I will admit that.  Laying down wires is not a cheap process so not too many new comers in this industry.  But I promise, the minute there is a new comer to our neighborhood with pretty good service, I will say good-bye to Comcast.  You do not have a loyal customer here.  Just one that needs your service.  Go Elon Musk.  Please start your next big adventure.  Google works too.
